After I have finished with you, my son, this book, which is the latest of my scientific works on medicine with the addition of this one, and has been completed in this way by the exposition of its contents and the declarations which are found in it, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this treatise which is a part of the art of surgery, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since surgery with the hand is a new art in our time and at a remote period: until perhaps its science has perished and its trace has been erased: nothing remains of it except for slight descriptions in the ancient books, which have been altered by the hand: and thereby there has arisen error and hesitation, until its intentions have been closed and its scope extended: It seemed to me that I should bring together in this treatise, according to order, its positions and declarations, and its brevity: and that I should explain the forms of the instruments of cautery and other instruments of the art, together with their addition and preparation which is necessary
However, it is not possible to find a good artisan of this art with his hand in our time: because the art of medicine is long, and the author must exercise himself beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen has narrated, until he knows the movements of the limbs, their forms, and their connection, and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, and lacerations, and the number of these things, and their emergence, and the pulsation of veins, and quietness, and the exit of places.
And for this reason Hippocrates said, that the name is much with the name, and little with the work, and especially in the art of the hand
We have indeed spoken of this at the beginning of this book.
For he who is ignorant of what we have said concerning anatomy will fall into error, and will thereby harm men. As for me, I have seen many who have learned of this science without study or experiment.
Since I have seen a stupid doctor attempt to remove a swelling from a woman's neck by cutting her arteries, and she died between his hands.
And I have seen another doctor who attempted to extract a stone from a patient's bladder, though the stone was large. He did this with the result that he extracted the stone along with the bladder itself And the man died on the third day.
And I myself was called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would certainly die.
And I have seen another doctor who was paid by a certain Duke of our land for his medical skill: and it happened to a black slave who was with him, that he fractured his leg near his heel: and the doctor, with his ignorance, bound the fracture with nails and strong stitching, and did not allow the wound to drain.
And as a result the slave died according to his desires. Then he dismissed him after a few days, and commanded him not to move his ligament: and he remained like that until the swelling of his leg had gone down, and his foot and leg, and as a result he died.
I was called to him again: and I found him perfectly calm and free from pain
And indeed corruption was confirmed in the limb: and I could not restrain it
When the limb has ceased to suffer corruption, it is no longer liable to further damage.
When the limb has ceased to suffer corruption, it is no longer liable to further damage.
When the limb has ceased to suffer corruption, it is no longer liable to further damage. That is, because when the cancer is pure and black, it does not require any further support, except in the limb which will tolerate it, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And thus, my son, you must know that an operation is divided into two parts: the one which is associated with health, and the one which carries the peril in various conditions.

But before we speak of any operation, it is necessary to mention the quality of the dressings and instruments: and in what complexions it should be used
I say therefore, that the discourse concerning the quality of the cautery dressing and its name is a prolonged, subtle, scientific, and secret discourse.
And many wise men have spoken on this matter, and they have differed among themselves: and indeed little is to be gained from their discourses, fearing the length of the discourse itself
I say therefore, that the cautery is useful for all complexions, whether with material or without material: except for two complexions which are the hot complexion without material, and the dry complexion without material
In the hot and dry complexions with material they disagree. Some indeed say that the cautery is harmful in these matters. Others have said otherwise, namely that Cauterium is not suitable for wounds caused by heat and dryness: for the nature of fire is heat. It is unsuitable to heal wounds caused by heat and dryness with heat and dryness.
Others have said the opposite, namely that Cauterium makes an ointment in all wounds caused by heat and dryness, which happen in the bodies of men: for when you compare the body of a man and moisten it, to the nature of fire, you find the body of a man chilled.
And I myself have learned from experience that this is true
It is not enough to learn only from this sermon; one must also learn from experience the last exercise of the Cauterium course, and have recognized the diversity of the dispositions of men, and the causes and accidents of their wounds, and their speed
Except in the cases of the most delicate complexions, there is no fear of them: and especially in the case of cold and moist wounds For all the physicians agree on this: and they do not hesitate to use Cauterium on them.
And behold, the sons of Alexander say that the secret of the treatment of wounds by Cauterium with fire, and the benefit of it over Cauterium with burning medicine is because fire is simple, whose action does not extend except to the part that is cauterized: and it does not harm any other connected limb except for a slight burn
The medicines of burning have an action that extends beyond the part that is cauterized: and perhaps makes it difficult to heal the wound of the limb, and perhaps even causes death.
Fire, however, on account of its subtlety and the excellence of its substance, does not cause this [pain], unless it be excessive.

And know this, my sons, that they themselves dissent in the time when it is necessary to make a cautery, and they say that it is better to leave it alone.</start_of_turn>

Do not let the minds of the learned or the sons think that because of this it is not useful, except for madmen and foolish doctors, for the ailment which is healed by a cautery is not always cured: they take this for consequence, and it is not so: for a cautery is not, except in the case of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries humors which are the causes of the ailments.</start_of_turn>
Truly, a cautery surpasses medicine by its speed of action, the excellence of its operation, and the certainty of its mastery: and it is possible that the ailment will be cured at some later time according to the complexion of the patient, the location of the ailment, and the excellence of the treatment: and that which is prepared in his body from the collection of superfluous humors in it: and that which comes to him from the cause itself, except in the case of an ailment in which a cautery is administered.</start_of_turn>

However, the thing is contrary to this, and the intention that the cautery is the last remedy in medicine is not true, except when we administer other modes of treatment for some ailment, and these do not yield: then we administer the cautery at the end, and it yields. It is thus that the cautery is the last remedy, not in accordance with the intention as the vulgar people and the multitude of doctors understand it.</start_of_turn>
The ancients said that the cautery with gold is better than the cautery with iron: and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold, and the fineness of its substance: and they said that it does not form pus at the place of the cautery.</start_of_turn However, this is not absolutely true: for I have seen this to be the case, and I have found that it does not cause this in some bodies without other things.</start_of_turn>

Concerning the care of these things that fall in autumn.
Everything that falls in autumn is of four kinds: either a mineral stone, or something like a stone, such as iron, or gold: or it is from a plant, such as lentil, and beans: or it is a fluid substance, such as water, and vinegar, and blood, or something similar to these things.
When such a stone or kind of stone is fallen in autumn which does not grow in autumn from the earth, it exposes the autumn to the sun: if you wash the stone, then distil from oil or vinegar something from the earth in autumn. And when the wound is healed even with the subtlest of cautery and incision: it is healed by fumigation, according to this method.</start_of_turn Take calamine, and hyssop, and origanum, and rue, and sassafras, and chamomile, and wormwood, and similar herbs: and mix them all together, or some of them in a pot, and immerse them in vinegar, and boil: and cover the pot with a lid: and put a hole in the middle of the pot, above which is made a concave instrument according to this method.</start_of_turn
Let air or metal enter: and the extremity is introduced into the cavity containing the pomegranate, until the vapor ascends to the upper opening of the cannula, until the opening is obscured by much.
Then repeat over the same [procedure] several times, until it heals.
And beware, do not perform this treatment in the beginning of an attack of inflammation. The procedure is useful only in a cold inflammation: and it must not be performed except when the inflammation has subsided.</start_of_turn>
If however this instrument is not present, then take a needle and make a hole in the extremity and introduce cork or resin: so that it does not burn the bone: because the cork or resin hinders the vapor from burning the bone: and this is a good treatment with safety.</start_of_turn>

Of the extraction of the blood vessel.

On the excision of the epiglottis from the apostemate within the guttur by chance.
On the excision of the epiglottis from the apostemate within the guttur by chance.
The ancients say that they performed this excision of the epiglottis in the guttur, and none of them in our land ever performed it: this is the report of their speech.
In cases of spasms, however, the excision of the epiglottis must be performed: when no other remedy proves effective: for all veins and the lung are weakened by this.
In those who have a hard swelling in the mouth, or gut, or two abscesses, when there is no inflammation in the channel, it is necessary to perform the excision of the epiglottis to escape from the impending destruction caused by the swelling
It is necessary therefore, when we wish to perform this, to cut through the epiglottis under three or four circles of the epiglottis, with a small incision through the thickness, in that place where there is cartilage between two circles as much as in the cartilage itself: and this is a suitable place for the incision, because it is bare of flesh and the blood vessels from it are long.

Chapter 52.
Of the care of the belly.
The belly swells from many wounds. Or from incisions of the intestines which are above the belly: and it comes out through the opening, or the intestine itself, according as it happens in other ruptures. Or from blood which flows from the vein, or from the artery, as has been said before Or from a distension of the belly itself.
If, however, it is due to a wound of the scrotum, and the opening of the tube: then the colour of the after-effect is similar to that of the body: and it is soft, without pain: and appears in various places. And if it is due to the emission of the intestine, then its place is as we have mentioned, with a greater degree of variety in its appearance. As you touch it with your fingers, it is hidden: then it returns, and sometimes there is a sound with it: and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath, and great pain ensues
If indeed it is due to moisture, it is soft: then it is not hidden when you touch it with your hand, neither is there constriction, nor does it swell.
If it is due to blood, then it appears with these signs: the after-effect is black as night at the root of the penis
If indeed it is due to flesh that has died: then the after-effect is thick, great, hard, and appears according to the quantity of one
If indeed it is due to swelling, then its touch is soft.
And the operation in this is as you consider: if the prominence of the navel is due to the artery, or the vein, or swelling: then you must abstain from treatment of it. Chapter 57.
Concerning the treatment of infants, and the care for an error from an accident.
Circumcision is not a continuous solution like other wounds: indeed when it is carried out by our operation, with our will, and when it is in children of their own kind, it is necessary to show in this operation a greater skill and to remove as little as possible of the surrounding area.
I say, therefore, that the ancients did not speak of circumcision in any of their books: for they did not use it in their practices, and there is nothing except that which we have learned through experience.
Indeed, for I have found a greater part of surgeons to be engaged in artificial methods, such as phlebotomy and cautery, using the knife with a nail and with scissors: and they employ them for all sorts of affections, and bind with thread and suture with a needle.
I have also tried all these methods, and I have not found a better method of healing than the use of scissors and thread binding.
For in the use of the knife with a nail, a great quantity of skin flees. For the skin of the prepuce has two layers: therefore it is possible that the upper skin may split, and the lower layer will be threatened: it is therefore necessary to make an incision to split the other, and to avoid the future pain And when the healing is done by means of the cautery, which is what the physicians use, the incision of the extremity of the limb is not secured: for perhaps it enters the opening of the canal.
But in the use of the needle with a hook, perhaps the iron will go through, and will corrupt your work: and the skin of a boy is of little strength, and many are produced in this way, which does not befit healing: I therefore reject this method
Healing by means of the knife and thread, however, has proved a good experiment to me: for the knives are proportional to the incision: therefore, as the former is greater, so also is the latter. When you have therefore grasped your hand, the two acutenesses are proportional, and they cut according to the operation of one at the same time: and it makes a similar compression of the figure, containing the skin of the member from all sides, so that no error is made at all
And the manner of performing the operation is thus, that you make the child understand, especially if there is one who understands fully, that you do not do this unless you bind the thread in its place: and you dismiss him until another day.
Then make him rejoice and be glad in every way that he can, from which he receives his intelligence. Then make him stand between your prepared hands, and do not sit down: and hide the shears in your sleeve or under your foot, so that the child sees nothing of them, neither anything of the instruments.
Then insert your hand into the wound, and blow into the skin, and draw it up, until the head of the wound comes out. Then bind up the rest that is gathered in that cavity.
Then bind the place marked with a double thread. Then bind below it with the same thread as before Then hold with your index finger and thumb the place of the lower binding securely, and cut between the two bindings. Then lift the skin up quickly and remove the head of the wound Then let the blood run slowly (for it is better thus) and put powder on it: and put a bandage over the powder on which the swollen part has been immersed in rose-water, pounded with fresh rose-water: and dismiss him until the next day: and care for the rest of the treatment until he is healed.
The form of the shears for this dressing is like this
There are two handles and two blades, and the handles should not extend into the wound: and the length of the two blades should be equal to the length of two thumbs together
An error often occurs in excision: because perhaps the entire intrinsic skin has escaped beyond the incision.
Therefore it is necessary to extend the time from your hour until your nail has passed beyond the margin of the wound: and then make the incision according to the degree of equality
If you are unable to hold the wound steady with your nail, then extract it with forceps and make the incision.
If, however, three days have passed and what remains under the swelling has become soft, remove the dressing: then let the swelling subside, and cleanse it gently, and make the incision as before: and take care to avoid the head of the swelling. It will not cause any damage to it.
Treat it with the care that consolidates the wound from its fragments, as we have narrated in the treatise on fragments: and if it happens that it breaks through the skin beyond the measure, and reaches the upper parts, it does not cause any damage to it even then
Treat it with the care we have mentioned, until it is healed

Of the extraction of a retained vein in a swelling
The retention of urine in the swelling is caused by a stone, or frozen blood, or pus, or flesh born, or similar things of that kind that we have mentioned in the section on treatment of diuresis.

It is formed of silver, is subtle, soft, and concave like a pennaceous quill in the smoothness of a ray, long like the palm of one hand and a half: which has a fine cannula in its head.
The way to evacuate the bladder is through itself: take two threads and tie them at their extremities with good ligature. Insert the extremity of the thread into the lower part of the siringa: and pierce with forceps if anything comes out through the wool. But insert into the cannula with certainty, as if lifting.

Then push the siringa into itself until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel that it has gone to the painful area: and do not do this except when the meatus through which it passes is tortuous
Then draw out the thread gradually with the wool The bladder will follow the wool.
Then draw out the urine, and make the bladder flow through the opening of the urine: and repeat the siringa, and do not cease doing this until the bladder is emptied, and the patient feels relief.

Chapter LX.
Â¶ On the extraction of the Lapis.
We have already spoken in the treatise on the species of the Lapis, and its treatment with physicians: and we have spoken of the difference between the Lapis generated in the bowels and the uesica, and the signs of the latter: and we have spoken of the Lapis in which the operation is performed with the hand and the section: and the Lapis which is generated in the uesica itself: and that which appears in the abscess. And I shall speak of this with manifest exposition and abbreviation.
I say therefore, that the Lapis which is generated in the uesica, most often happens to children
And from its signs it is known that the urine comes out of the uesica like water in its substance: and there appears in it white sand, and the patient feels his wound swelling and throbbing, and he groans with it, and is often fainting Then it is erected, and goes out with the anus in many people.
Healing is easy for children from this point on until they are fourteen years old. It is difficult in old age. But in youth it is middle-aged; for that which is between these two is of medium kind: and that which is greater in age, the cure is easier: and if it is slight, the care is less expensive
When we come to the cure, it is necessary in the first place to purge the patient with a cathartic, which will evacuate all the stool which is in the intestines: for this indeed often hinders the finding of the stone during inquiry
Then the patient is taken with his feet, and is beaten, and moved downwards: so that the stone may go down to the bottom of the bladder, or may come out from a high place somewhat.
Then make him sit between your hands prepared, and your hands be under his buttocks, so that the bladder may be entirely inclined downwards
Then inquire of him, and touch him externally.
If you feel the stone in the space, then immediately perform a section above it
If it does not come under your touch at all, then you must remove the index finger of your left hand if the patient is a child: or the middle finger if he is an adult male: and insert it into his rectum, and inquire of the stone, until it is under your finger: and bring it slowly to the neck of the bladder.
Then press above it with your finger, and push it outwards towards the place where the incision is to be made: and command the minister to grasp the bladder with his hand, and command another minister to extend the testicles of his hand to the upper part: and another hand to move the skin which is under the testicles in the part where the incision is to be made.
Then introduce the sponge into the wound, which has this shape. Then introduce the sponge into the wound, which has this shape. Find in it what is between the womb and the testicles, and not in the middle, at the side of the left hip: and let the incision be above the highest stone, and your finger be in the rectum: and make a transverse incision, so that the external incision is wide and the internal incision is narrow, according to the quantity that it is possible for the stone to issue from it not greater.
Perhaps the finger that is in the rectum will be compressed by the stone at the incision, and will issue without difficulty.
And you know that the stone has angles and margins, because of which its exit is difficult
And from this [stone] is soft, like a gland, and round: and its exit is easy
Therefore, to the stone which has angles and margins, add in the fissure
If it does not issue thus, then you must know that you must place something above it: or that you must grasp it with a forceps with a handle like the moon, which grasps the stone and does not slip from it: or that you must introduce an instrument under it, curved at its extremities.
If you cannot do this, then enlarge the opening nearby. If anything else flows out from the blood, cut it off with a saw
If there is more than one stone, then push out the big one first to the bone of the hip Then cut over it Then push out the small ones afterwards: and do the same if there are more than two.
If the wound is great, then ignorance is equal to the section above it. For if a sick man is seized by two things, either he will die, or he will suffer a persistent discharge of urine: because the place is not consolidated anywhere.
But give him an enema to expel it, until it comes out: or take hold of the fracture of it with forceps, until you have driven it out frustrated.
When you have finished your operation, then put on a coverlet, and aloe, and dragon's blood: and bind it up, and put upon it a soft dressing of oil and wine, or rose water and cold water: so that the swelling may subside
Then rest the sick man on his side, and do not relax the ligaments, until the third day. When you have relaxed it, stitch up the place with much water, and oil.
Then care for it with rue balm, and alum, until it heals.
If indeed in the wound there is added a soft swelling, and corruption, and such like: as if blood is congealed in the bladder, and is withheld from it: and this is known from the discharge of blood with urine. Insert your finger into the wound, and draw out the clot of blood. For if it remains, it causes corruption of the bladder, and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar, and water, and salt: and apply all kinds of things which are useful for the cure, until it heals
And it is necessary in the course of the cure of all these things, that you bind up two thighs, and bind together, the cause of the physicians who put things upon the place.
If the stone is small and lies in the bladder, and it projects into it, and prevents the discharge of urine: then care for it with that which I have mentioned before until you reach the section. You must not evacuate from the section for this treatment, for I have proved it to be effective.</start_of_turn>
And it is that you take a perforator of iron, which is triangular at the extremities, acute, and fixed in wood.</start_of_turn>
Then take a thread, and tie it with it under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.</start_of_turn
Then insert the perforator into the bladder with ease, until it reaches the stone: and withdraw the perforator gradually from the stone: and make the perforation through it from the other side.</start_of_turn
The urine will immediately cease.</start_of_turn>
Then press your hand over that which remains from the stone from the exterior part of the bladder.</start_of_turn It will itself break, and go out with the urine, and the infirm will be healed.</start_of_turn>
If however this treatment is not prepared for him, because of something that hinders it: then tie a thread under the stone, and a thread above the stone.</start_of_turn Then dry over the stone in the very urine between two ligatures.</start_of_turn Then extract it.</start_of_turn> Then dissolve the ligament, and bind the frozen blood, which is in the wound.</start_of_turn>
And it is not necessary to tie a thread under the stone, except that it does not return to the bladder: and to tie one above, except when the thread is dissolved after the evacuation of the stone, the skin returns to its place, and closes the wound: and for this reason it is necessary for you to tie that above when you have ligated the thread below, so that you elevate the skin to the upper parts, so that the skin returns to its proper place and closes the wound, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
On the extraction of the stone from women.
On the extraction of the stone from women.
Stones are rarely generated in women.
If, however, it should happen to any of them that a stone should occur, then its treatment is difficult, and is prohibited by many methods
One of them is: perhaps the woman is pregnant.
And the second is, because you will not find a woman who will confess to a physician that she has a stone when she is chaste, or out of fear of her husband
The third is, because you will not find a woman who is well-informed concerning this art, especially the operation with the hand
And the fourth is the distance of the stone from the place of its origin: because it demands a deep section, and there is fear in that
If necessity compels you to do that, then you must take a woman physician, who is well-informed: and few are found
If you do wish to do this beforehand, then seek out a wise physician, discreet, and present to her a skilled woman in matters concerning women, or a woman who has been trained in this art to a certain extent: make her do everything that you have learned from your inquiry concerning the stone
Firstly, that she may see if the woman is pregnant: then she must insert her finger into her belly and search for the stone
If she finds it, she should grasp it under her finger and then command the midwife to insert her finger into the lower belly, and inquire about the stone after she has placed her left hand over the waist and has pressed it firmly

And if they do not go out with that, then gradually reduce the foot, until you have set it according to the natural form For it will go out of itself when its time comes.
If it is opposed by all this, then take hold of the upper part of the wound with the thumb and index finger, and with the other hand take a sponge dipped in oil and gum Arabic: and strike all over the wound with a good blow: then lay over it the palm of the woman's hand, and the lower part of her belly. Then make him sit in warm water, until the hypocondria follows
When the lower parts are relaxed by the warmth, then make him drink a mixture of myrrh: and put him to bed. When an hour has passed, then make him sit on a seat. Then make him draw in: and bind his jaw and nose: and press the lower part of the belly with ease For the foot will go out immediately.
The foot comes out over the knee and hand. When it comes out in this form, then put your hand in slowly Then the woman lies down on his neck, and hangs his feet down: and she herself lies down on the bed, and puts her hands together Then first above the belly of it slowly. Then withdraw that which is under its feet from the heel, until it is prepared in the lower part. If the fetus does not come out, then grasp its feet and move them by movement of the hand Then first above the navel slowly, until the fetus ascends to the upper part Then insert your hand inside, and stabilize the fetus slowly: and command the woman to compress, until the fetus comes out.
The fetus comes out lying sideways from the hands It is finished with the reduction of its hand If however it is not possible to reduce it, then elevate the woman, and make her walk
If she is indeed unable to walk, then make her lie down on the bed: and strike her thighs with the hand of the other hand
Then administer the unguents which you prepared from the mucilage.
If she bears a part, then make her sit on a seat Then stay in the reduction of the hand, and stabilize the fetus according to the natural figure: and command the woman to compress, and tell her to breathe, until it comes out
The fetus comes out over its collar, with its hands spread out, and its face is towards the back of the mother The midwife must hold the foot of the fetus, then slowly turn it around, and stabilize it with ease
When it is thus stabilized, then place over its vulva what we have mentioned of the wax and mucilage
Then command him to move slowly. When you have done that, then make him sit down on a chair, and command him to lean to his right side. Then command him to breathe: and make him clench his abdomen with his hand
The fetus is prepared on the right side When it has descended to the birth opening in this way with the second hand, then cut the second one with your nail until it is evacuated from the moisture.
If it is suspended on the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it does not remain and die
Then push the fetus inwards, until you place your hand according to what is necessary: and command the woman to compress herself slightly: I myself will come out through the easy way.
The birth of twins, or many fetuses. You know that twins are often born: and sometimes three or four are born. This is extraordinary, and rarely happens.
Five or more is a thing beyond nature, and does not endure: and it contains these [fetuses] which, although multiplied, are one: and they are separated by the navel cord of each of them
And sometimes they come out like a single fetus through a natural birth: easily: and sometimes they come out through an unnatural birth, as we have said.
If there are any difficulties with some of them at the birth, and they arrive at that which we have mentioned from unnatural figures, then care for them as we have said: and let the midwife be gentle, and do what she does with ease and delay, and adapt to every figure as she is prepared for it from the ingenuity guiding her to safety
Remember that its formation is in the womb from embryos, and it is aborted.
When it is formed in the womb, one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and many ten: and I have seen that a woman has aborted seven, and another fifteen, all of them being formed
Since it is established by the measurement of a glorious wise man.
Therefore all this must be known in the science of Obstetrics. Perhaps it will come to the like of this: let it be opposed to that which must be opposed to it.
Chapter LXXVI.
Of the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you care for a dead fetus with medicine as I have said in the discourse, and it does not go out, and you must do it by operation with the hands, then you must consider
If a healthy woman is virtuous, and there is no other cause for fear of loss of life: then you must cause the woman to lie down over the bed, over her back, and let her head be inclined downwards, and her legs be raised: and the minister should hold the patient firm from two parts, or bind her to the bed, so that her body is not pulled out during the extraction of the fetus
Then moisten the os matricis with oily things with high mucilage, with alum, and poppy seed meal.
Then let the Obstetrician wet his hand with these things and oils: then he will introduce it into the womb with ease Then seek the place where the nails of the fetus are fixed, and the convenient place for it
Consider therefore at all times, if the fetus is prepared to descend upon his head: then fix the hooks in his eyes, or in his neck, or in his mouth, or in his palate, or under his beard, or in his armpits, or in the nearby parts of his ribs, and under his navel.
If he has descended upon his feet, then in the flanks and the middle ribs.
It is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand: and place the curvature of his hand in that which is between the left thumb and little finger: and introduce it with the thumb with ease, and fix the hook in some of those places which we mentioned until it reaches the desired thing
Then fix the other or the third hook, if necessary: so that there is an equal tension, and it does not incline to one side.
Then extend the extension equally, and do not let it extend only according to the rule of the straight line, but move it to all parts, so as to alleviate his exit: just as it is done with a tooth when extracting it.
And it is necessary at that point to soften the extension. Which if it is retained from that part, then it is necessary for the obstetrician to grasp some of his fingers with his thumb and introduce them from the side, so that he may rotate with what is retained
If therefore his part of the fetus comes out, then exchange the hooks to another place which is higher: do this until the whole fetus comes out
If therefore his hand comes out before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it because of its adhesion: then it is necessary to cover over his hand with the palm of the hand Then extract the thumb when it goes out, either at the joint of the thumb and the palm, or in the cubit: and so it should be done in the other hand, and in both feet.
If however the head of the fetus is large, or if there is a constriction in its exit, or if there is water in its head: then it should be introduced between the fingers of Spatumile spinosum, and find with it the head, and extract the water: or break it with the instrument which is called Almisdac: whose form comes with the forms of the other instruments in the following chapter.
Likewise do this if the fetus is of great head size: then it should be severed with the clamp: or extract it with the hook, as we have said. Then draw out the bones with forceps.
When the head comes out, and is caught at the collar: then it is found, until the humidity which is in the chest is discharged
If however it does not become complicated, neither obeys the exit: then cut off the head roughly, as much as possible for you
If however the lower belly is apostemated, or there is water in it: then it should be perforated, until the humidity comes out from it.
If however the fetus is above his feet: then its traction is easy, and its direction to the maternal bone is smooth
If however it is constricted in the belly, or the chest: then it should be extracted with the cloth which you have covered over your hand: and find the belly, or the chest, until it comes out naturally
If however the rest of the limbs are delivered, and the head returns: then the Obstetrix puts in his left hand. If any opening is found in the matrix, then the hand is introduced into the depth of the matrix, and it grasps with the head, and pulls it until it reaches the os of the matrix. Then one or two hooks are introduced into it, and it is pulled with them.
If the os of the matrix is closed, because of a thick clot that has happened to it: then it is not necessary to toil over it, rather it is necessary to administer an effusion of moist things, fats: and administer plasters. And sit in the waters that soften and moisten them.
If the fetus is above its side, then it is possible to equalize it: then the thing which we said concerning the fetus above is administered for it
If it is not possible to do this, then a perforation is made carelessly, and it is extracted
And it is necessary that you do not let anything escape from the second part altogether.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we said concerning the cold clots which happen in the matrixes.
If blood flows, then descend into the styptic waters, and administer the rest of the treatment.
And I myself have seen a woman in whom there was a dead fetus: then it was impregnated over her again with oil, afterwards the other fetus also died. It happened to her after a long time that a clot formed in her navel, and it became inflated, until it opened: and pus began to emit from it.
I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time: and it did not consolidate.
I placed over it some strong-adhesive plaster: and it came out from its place. Then some days passed by, and another bone was discharged. I am amazed at this, for there is no bone within.
I think therefore, because there were dead bones of a fetus within.
I asked the woman, and she extracted many bones from me, which were in a better position: and I did so without pain for a long time, and I sent out a little pus from that place.
And I did not touch this foreign thing, except that there is knowledge in it, and help for that which the skilled physician gives with his hands from the art of healing.

And these two additions are introduced into the matrix bone, so that it opens when you rotate the two rings.

Head LXXVIII
About the extraction of the Second
When the Second is retained in the part, then it is necessary to grasp the lower part, in order to retain the breath Then make the incision with the forceps: and grasp the hand over his jaw, and take hold of his breath. If he comes out through this, that is good
If not: then grasp his head, and pierce in the middle of the cheek: and place in it herbs that open the bone like fennel, rue, and plantain, and chamomile, and hyssop, and cassia twig, and centaury: grasp all these herbs, or some of them, and immerse them with water, and place them over fire.

It will then obey, and be restored, and depart from the adhesion.
As for the os of the belly being closed [i.e., contracted], as we have mentioned: care for it with sternutation, and from an oil medication with herbs.
If, however, it does not depart with all that we have mentioned: then beware lest you tire yourself out in the course of the extraction process.
It is true that it should depart from the os of the belly to the woman's hip. Then administer an enema with four drugs. This will cause the belly to soften after a few days, and dissolve, and depart
Indeed when it has putrefied, it will emit a foul smell from the belly and head, and will cause pain which will make the patient weak. It is necessary therefore that suitable fumigations be administered for this.
Some of the ancient experts are experienced in fumigation with nasturtium and dried figs.

Chapter 79.
Concerning the care of an unpierced animal
Many boys are born with their nails unpierced, whom I have seen to have been oiled with subtle saffron. It is necessary therefore that the midwife pierce that nail with her finger: and if not, pierce it with the pointed Spatumili: and beware tears, lest it touch him
Then put upon it infused wool in wine and oil. Then care for it with the nails, until it is healed.

Chapter 80
Concerning the care of fistulas which happen in the lower part
Fistulas which happen in the lower part are Nodulation and Swelling which happen near any limb: or in the space of one part: and there is one fistula, or more
When the old Nodatio is relaxed, it opens and white watery moisture or subtle pus issues from it.
Or when there are penetrating fistulas from them. They are recognized by that which comes out with the discharge and by swelling, when the patient is in pain: and perhaps comes out with worms.
There are fistulas when they extend from the penetrating area to the cavity or to the muscle of the belly And from the penetrating area to the hip joint, and to the knot of the tailbone
From this, however, it is recognized that the penetrating fistula is known until it reaches the anus, even if it is not penetrating, as when you insert your finger into the anus: and you insert a needle sub-externally into the fistula from outside.
If there is a twist in it, then introduce in the gut a lead needle or a hair from a horse's tail until you feel the needle or hair, or until the hair comes out on your finger
If you do not feel the needle itself, neither that anything comes out with the discharge, neither swelling, neither worms as I have said: then you know that it is not penetrating: take care of the cure then.
When the fistula is penetrating until the cavity or the bladder muscle: then its meaning is the discharge of urine from it, and the prohibition of this so that the place may be consolidated with the physicians.
When it is penetrating until the hip joint or the hip bone: then its sign is that the attempt reaches up to this point, if there is no twist up to the bone: and a sensation of pain in the circumference of the part, and that pus always comes out from it: and that there is no benefit in it from the medication, neither is it consolidated with oil
In these penetrating fistulas, there is no complete cure: the cure is toil and perseverance from the stupid doctors who form them.
In these non-penetrating and non-ancient fistulas, healing is expected with a clamp: as I have said before, and as I have proved: let the patient lie between your hands over his belly: elevate his limbs until above his knees, and let his knees bend towards his belly Then introduce lead or air into the fistula, if there is a tortuousness in the fistula, until you know where it ends.
If, however, the patient feels around the belly, then you must introduce your finger into the belly.
If you feel in your finger that it is attempting to penetrate through the recognized area, except for what you feel between your finger and the flesh, or carrion: then you know for certain that it is penetrating: there is no work in this, because it is not its cure, as we have said
They say that in some people, the cure is in the flesh itself, and from the medicine which is expected to be applied: thus you should apply gentle cautery under the breadth of the fistula, as has been said before, and introduce the flame itself into the fistula until it disappears from around the belly Then do this twice or thrice, until you know that all the fatty flesh which is similar to the veins of a bird's wing has been consumed by the filter.
Then care for it with buttered bandages until those fatty tissues have gone: then care for it with unguents that generate flesh and consolidate.
If it heals well, that is good.
If not, it does not recover with any other treatment at all.
If not, it does not recover even if you take away the finger that is in the groin and that is between the thumb and the fleshy swelling from the bone, or if you lance it: and you should know that if you do this, dry the skin from the start of the fistula, and take away the fleshy swelling with the thumb that is in the fistula, until the drying out reaches the end of the swelling, and the fleshy swelling is freed.
Then wash the surrounding flesh thoroughly, so that no pus remains from the cannula of feathers of birds.
If, however, blood flows and mixes with you and the operation, so that you must cut through the flesh: then it is better that you cauterize with fire or with acute medicine.
For indeed, cauterization with fire unites the good habits, brings together the added flesh, and stops bleeding, and dries up moisture
Then care for it with cloths dipped in butter, or with bruised grapes, until the place discharges pus, and the added flesh is expelled in the pus.
Then care for it with solid bandages, containing substances that promote the formation of tough flesh: and these are medicines that have stypticity and drying qualities.
For when it is healed, then it is cured: and not by doing it repeatedly.
If, however, the fistula has persisted to the depth of the abdomen, and has become prolonged by the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the abdomen and inquire about it
If you feel the fleshy swelling and between you and the fistula is close to penetration: then there is no operation in this case, except according to the degree of trust and hope
Whatever is done by one of three methods: either by cauterizing it as we have said; or by dissecting it until its concavity is complete, so that one may afterwards insert instruments and perform the cure. Proceed not too far with the dissection, lest you cut through the membrane of any organ, and cause an unfavorable outcome of the evacuation without the will of the patient Then care for that which we have said.
Perhaps it will recover: or you may stretch the membrane and cleanse it when dry, as we have said, or with hooks, or with some other sharp instrument. Then cleanse the excised tissues which are in the dissection, until fat remains only with the scarp.
Then endeavor to restore the entire wound with the dissection, and the upper orifice where it is closed: and there will remain an open fistula in the inner part of the anus, and it will be easier over the infirmity.
And when the fistula is sutured in this way: that is, when you insert a hook into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the skin and the margin of the anus: then grasp the hook with the perforating extremity, which is like a needle, that is, prepared for cutting the skin, in this shape And insert into it a thread of silk wound from five threads, and pass it around it. Then insert the hook with the thread into the fistula, until its concavity is complete
If, however, it is penetrating into the inner margin of the anus, then draw out the thread from that hole: so that you may insert your finger into the anus, and draw out the extremity of the thread, and join the two extremities together: and bind them so that neither slips, and leave it like that for one day, or two days: and the more the thread has penetrated the flesh, the better you must bind it, until those parts of the flesh which are between the two extremities of the thread have become soft and fallen away: then care for the wound, until it is consolidated and healed
If the opening of the Fistula is not penetrable: then make it so in whatever way is prepared for you, except that it be in great depth. Except that it be in great depth, make it so in whatever way is prepared for you
Except that it be in great depth, make it so in whatever way is prepared for you until it is healed.
The form of the spindle which is found in the Fistula, whose curvature is acute upwards and the other part is not acute, so that it does not damage that which is not necessary, like urine.

Head wounds without bone fracture.
I have already spoken concerning the treatment of wounds in general, which is contained in the book. Here I will speak of the treatment of these wounds with the hand and with the aid of physicians according to their custom
Wounds are of various kinds according to the cause of the wound and the place where the wound has fallen
Wounds are thus of various kinds, as when caused by a stone, or by a sword or knife, or by a blow with a spear or wood or arrow, or by like things
Wounds which are caused in different parts of the body are also of various kinds, as for example a wound which falls on the head, or the neck, or the chest, or the stomach, or the limb: or like those on the joints
And I will speak of the treatment of other wounds, so as to give the reason and rule concerning the rest of the wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds: for the memory of the compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say thus. When a simple wound occurs in the head and there is no fracture of the bone: then consider whether it is from a stone or something similar. Then break only the skin: and the wound is great and the time for the inflammation of the surrounding area is great: then proceed with care and perform a cephalic phlebotomy immediately: do not delay this: and extract from him from the blood according to the quantity of his virtue. If there is anything which prohibits phlebotomy, especially if there is little blood flowing from the wound, do not do it And let the bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part.

Method of applying powdered gypsum. Recipe: mix one part of olive oil, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unburnt lime: grind them all together, and make a paste: apply it to the wound, and bind it securely, until it adheres well to the wound itself and is clotted with blood.

Of wounds of the belly, and the exit of the intestine, and the issue of them.</start_of_turn
The disruption which happens from inside is great, middle, or small.
It is great when the intestine or the number of intestines comes out from the great one
Therefore there is an introversion of the bowels, and the suture is more difficult and arduous
And the small disruption is also difficult in another way Therefore, it follows that the reduction is more difficult if you do not properly perform the introversion back to its place immediately: because it swells, opens, and swells up: and thus the entrance of it becomes difficult.
Therefore, the middle disruption is better: because with this one the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is with the two other kinds
You know that the suture of the belly is according to four methods.
Two sutures are common in the suture of the belly, and in the suture of the remaining wounds of the body: and two other sutures are proper for the rest of the wounds. However, there are other methods which are more proper for the suture of the belly: and I will narrate one of them with its exposition and declaration
I say, because when the wound is small, and something from the intestine comes out of it, and it is difficult to reduce it: then it is for one of the two methods. Either because of the smallness of the disruption, as we said: or because of the inflation of the intestine due to the cold of the air
When it is like this, then one must warm it up, so that you may immerse a sponge or a wet towel in warm water Or boil them in water a little bit, and cypress, and fennel, and embroil with them the intestines, until the swelling is resolved.
When it makes that liquid in which there is stickiness: it is better than plain water in resolving the swelling.
When you have thus resolved the swelling, then moisten the intestines with the water in which they have been boiled, either high or low. For thus it alleviates its entrance with a small thing.
If, however, its return is delayed after this treatment, then find in slight disruption, with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared than the section: and does not cause a pressing need to cut after necessity and the fault of the instrument.
Let one part be sharp and acute, and the other part not acute: and the extremity should not be fine like that of Spatumilis, but rather obtuse like a bean: and this is what resembles a wound, like the liquid
When the wound is thus strengthened, and the intestine is introduced, then it should be brought about that there is a reduction of it according to its natural form in its own place, if possible over that: because that is better
When indeed the disruption is wide in the lower part of the belly: then it should be made to lie flat on its back, and place its knees higher than its head. And if it is in the upper part of the belly, then place its head, and its chest higher than its lower parts
And similarly if there is a disruption in two parts of the belly, then place your intention and your consideration always in this, that the part in which the wound is should be higher than the other part.
It is thus necessary that the surgeons perform this work in large wounds and in medium wounds.
In small wounds, however, place this [dressing] according to what is prepared for you
Then make it so that your hands rest comfortably between your fingers, which hold the entirety of the hand together: and gather its lips together. Then draw out from it [the wound] whatever follows the suture one thing after another: and this is the manner of common suture of one
And it is necessary that you take an awl, or the number of awls according to the quantity of the wound's breadth. Then withdraw from the edge of the disruption the quantity of the finger of the hand, namely the physician: and fix the awl one beyond which you enter into the skin in two extremities of the skin, with two extremities of fat which is under the skin from the inside, until you make it penetrate from another side, and you gather together two extremities of the skin and two extremities of fat: and there are four orders thus formed
Then bind with a double thread around the circumference of the awl several times from two parts together, until two lips of the wound are gathered together by a decent aggregation.
Then withdraw the length of the finger also, and fix in the flesh another awl: afterwards tighten the skin with the thread, as you did with the first awl. Do not cease to do this until you have completed the constriction of the whole wound
And the middle awls between the length and the thickness: because the fine awls slip easily through flesh: and the thick ones are difficult to enter the skin: for this reason it is necessary that they be of middle thickness in the skin, and thick
It is not permissible that a needle should remain in two contiguous parts of the skin for a long time: for the flesh will otherwise quickly decay and a wound will open before consolidation has taken place, and will not be lengthened even when sutured, for it will be prevented from consolidating by the suture.
Then pierce the extremity of the needle, so that it does not wound the patient during sleep: and place wool pads around the needle from all sides, which will hold the needle in place: and draw it out, until you know that the wound has consolidated
And this is the kind of suture which is most suitable for small wounds For indeed one, or two, or several needles suffice in a suture.
The second common suture is that in which four extremities are bound together: two of the skin and two of the fat in one wound, with the needle through which the thread is passed being equal in thickness and consistency.
Then when you have pierced with the needle the four extremities, reduce the needle from the part from which you began, so that the thread be drawn out from the upper part of the wound: so that the suture be like the stitching of cloth. Place between every suture as much thickness as the breadth of a little finger
This kind of suture they know already.

Regarding care of ulcers and fistulas.
You know that every wound, or abscess when it grows old and decays, becomes an ulcer, and does not consolidate, and emits pus always, and does not heal: then it is called a fistula in every member in which it occurs.</start_of_turn>
And a fistula is indeed a filtered node, hard, white: with which there is no pain, which has the shape of a wing of a bird: and for this reason they call some of them Risati, that is, wings.</start_of_turn
And sometimes in wet weather it emits pus.</start_of_turn> And sometimes the humidity breaks in some hours.</start_of_turn And when this humidity is great and little, and is large and thin.</start_of_turn
And I say in general that any wound that does not heal, neither is born in this body, is not due to anything other than one of these causes.</start_of_turn
When one of these things is absent, either because of the scarcity of blood in the body, or because of its malice, or because between it and the lips there is a hard substance which hinders the natural growth of flesh, or because of the presence of many ulcers and pus, or because an ulcer in itself is putrid, and the matter which issues from it is of bad quality, or because the medicine is inappropriate for its treatment, or because there is corruption descending in the region which is a kind of pestilence, or by a peculiarity in the region, like that which occurs in Caesaraugusta, in which there is difficult digestion of food and a delay in its healing after a wound, by nature itself: or because in that place there is but one bone, or a number of bones.
And I have mentioned all these causes and signs of them, and their treatments with physicians. It is necessary for you to write here the treatment of fistula and stone, which is done by one operation with the hand.
You know therefore that fistula can occur in all parts of the body. There are fistulas which extend to great veins and arteries, or nerves, or the bladder, or the intestines, or the belly, or to some bones: or to some part of the backbone, or to some joint composed of several bones, such as the hand and foot. And there are those which arise from nearby parts of the great limb and are similar to these
Therefore, the fistulas of this kind are caused by difficult healings and do not receive treatment, and are associated with labor and ignorance
If however there is any fistula which does not extend to these places which I have mentioned, and if you hope and trust in its treatment, and wish to reach an understanding of it, then attempt to close it by air or by iron, since the fistula follows the straight line. Ask for help with it.</start_of_turn>
If, however, in the fistula there is a twist, then investigate it with a fine lead weight. Since lead with its softness conforms to the body, and curves around the twist
When there are many holes in the fistula, it is not possible to indicate the upper part with a hook It is necessary therefore to explore from the holes towards the holes.
For the moisture which fills the fistula, comes out through other holes, and runs from the holes.
Then inquire diligently in what way it is possible: whether it is bone or nerve, and whether the fistula is of great or little depth: or whether the fistula is one which has many holes, and lies above all that with the sum of your strength: with your questioning of the patient and the finding of pain on compression with your hand at the place, and similar signs and symptoms following.
When you have stood on all these stations truly, then go on to the treatment with confidence: and it is that you consider at that time if the fistula is close to the surface or far from the junction, or from a nerve, an artery, a vein, or a place which I have mentioned: then dry the fistula according to what has been said before from my narration, and remove what is in it from the filtration, and corrupt flesh, which is born in its orifice from the flesh, or pus, and like things: and care for it until it is healed
If, however, the fistula is of great depth and is according to the rule: then it is necessary to dissect it as deep as possible. Then remove from it all the corrupt flesh from it.

Then restore the limb with the unguents which produce healthy flesh, until it is healed

If indeed the small bone is corrupted, and it is possible for you: draw it out with fine forceps which are suitable for that.</start_of_turn>

And I tell you what happened to me in my leg: that you may take it as an example and an assistant for your operation
A youth of about thirty years of age suffered pain in his leg, because something had moved above the middle of his body inwards, that is, from within, until it reached the leg, and there was a large swelling: and there was no external cause for it.
It has been extended for a long time with an error of the doctors, until the swelling was opened, and many materials came out with it.</start_of_turn> And after that the cure was delayed, until the leg was bandaged, and many holes were made in it: which all emitted pus and moistened the body.</start_of_turn>
They treated him for a long time with many doctors, for two years at least, but there was no skill in their art, until I saw him and washed his leg and the things which were coming out of his holes were of great size: even all the men of the place fainted, and his colour was pale.</start_of_turn>
They attempted to reach one of the holes in his body, and they reached the bone.
Then I examined all the holes: and I found that they were all communicating with each other from all parts of the leg.</start_of_turn
I treated him accordingly, and I closed up one of the holes, until I found a piece of bone: and I found that it was corrupted: for it was rotten, putrefied, and perforated, until it had penetrated as far as the marrow.</start_of_turn
I saw that what had been detected was prepared from the rotten bone.</start_of_turn
And I concluded that there was no soundness in the bone except for that corruption, which I cut off and cauterized.</start_of_turn And I cured him of it.</start_of_turn>
Then I place restoration of the wound with the physicians consolidated in a spacious area. It is not consolidated yet.</start_of_turn>
Then I tried again, and I found upon the second examination above the first detection: and I found continuous corruption with the bone: and I saw that what appeared to me from that corruption also appeared from the corruption itself.</start_of_turn>
Then I attempt to restore it.</start_of_turn It is not restored.</start_of_turn
I found it therefore upon the third time above all, and I did not cease to cut the bone piecemeal, and to try to restore it: and it is not restored, until I cut through the bone round about the palm of the hand, and I extracted that with its marrow.</start_of_turn
Then I restored it with the physicians, and it was consolidated quickly, and healed: and no further operation was necessary for this purpose, except for the disposition of the infirmity of the patient, and his little tolerance, and my fear of death for him, because it was threatening him in every hour from the excessive evacuation of his bowels.</start_of_turn

About the cutting over an abscess Nakir.
This ailment is called in our land Nakir: and it is a pain which occurs in some limb: then it changes from limb to limb
And I myself have seen it happen, as I have told you I was called to a woman who was sick in some house. And I saw her arm and I found swelling in the armpit of the arm
And after an hour had passed I saw another swelling rise up like a worm, going up to the shoulder of her more quickly than is possible: like silver that is running from one place to another
The pain therefore departed from that place and was fixed in the shoulder
Then after an hour it ran through the rest of the body, until it reached the other arm
And she told me that it returned throughout her whole body, as I saw
I am amazed at the speed of its change from limb to limb And I myself had never seen such an ailment before like this, in this way But I have heard of many people who suffer from this pain which changes from limb to limb: and I have never seen it with my own eyes like I saw it in this woman
I do not think that is the case, except insofar as a woman has been among those from whom the stones have been detected in the belly: from this therefore it appears that the sense of smell has been transposed.
It is necessary that they do not appear according to this ratio in those who are delicate and have moist bodies, and in whom the veins are hidden
When therefore you see that the patient feels pain in that place, and that the wound appears to him: then if it is seen by the eye, as we have said, then grasp above and below that which is quicker: and dry above that, until the enclosed moisture is driven out: and cauterize the place.</start_of_turn>

For indeed the parts of this art and the distinctions of these matters are not comprehended by narration: neither is it comprehended by this book, nor by a prudent craftsman who compares few things with many: and with that which is present, with that which is absent: and he finds a new operation and a new instrument among the descent of all these matters when they happen.
I say therefore, that arrows do not go out of the parts in which they are fixed, except according to two ways. Except by attraction from the place from which it entered Or by turning back the other part
And that which comes out from where it entered, or the arrow proceeding in the flesh: it is attracted and comes out
If it does not yield to the outlet at the hour when it falls: then it is necessary that you discharge it for a few days, until the corruption of the flesh surrounding it has taken place: and thereby you will allay its attraction and its egressio.
If it hangs in bone, and does not yield to you at the outlet, then you must also discharge it for a few days: and do it again every day with its attraction and motion, until it comes out entirely
If it does not yield to you after days, then you must perform an incision all around the arrow in the very bone with fine silk, until the arrow is fully loosened Then draw out the arrow and extract it.
If however the arrow has vanished from its place in the body, and is hidden and concealed from sense: then inquire about it with care If you feel it, then draw out the arrow with some instruments that are suitable for its attraction.
If, however, you are unable to perform the procedure above due to the constriction of the wound or because of the length of the arrow in depth: and there is neither bone nor nerve nor fat there: then find above the wound until the wound is enlarged and the arrow can be extracted.
If there are any ligaments which hold the flesh fixed in the bone, then release the flesh from every side by all means, by any skill you are able, and the ingenuity which you can bring to bear, if you are unable to perform the evacuation of the flesh by fracture of the bone and rotation of the ear, until it becomes loose
And when you perform the extraction of the arrow, in whatever place it is, then use the twist of your hand with the forceps to all parts, until you make the wound discharge: and with the last slight tension, so that the arrow does not break, and that it is difficult for you to draw it, and for its own extraction.
If you are unable to perform it from one hour, then let it rest for a few days, until the things around it have decayed Then do it again: for it is in vain that you do it if it causes the flow of blood. Then administer what we have said from the treatment in its chapter: and guard your virtue from the incision of the vein, or nerve, or cord.
And administer all your skill in every way that you can in order to perform the extraction of the arrow: and let this be with ease, and tranquility, or slowly, and firmly, as I have told you
It is necessary that you do as you pull out the arrow, that the patient be in the same position as when the arrow was in him. Because of the great pain. If it is not possible for you to do this, then administer what is possible from the figures.
If it proceeds from the opposite side, or if anything proceeds from that towards the exterior: or it makes the extremity of the arrow bulge outwards by means of a sensation from the part of the skin which is close above, and it causes the juice to rise: dry therefore above that, and make a section according to the quantity which they take in that.
Then draw out the arrow: for itself makes the evacuation easy.
If however it remains in the bone, then turn your hand according to the roundness, until you press the arrow into the bone, and expand it for itself: then draw it out
And if not: leave it for a few days: then do it again, until it comes out naturally.
If the arrow-shaft is in that, then push it out with that (the hand).
If however the shaft has broken, and you wish to administer an impulse: then introduce an instrument with a concave surface into the cavity, so that the concavity of the instrument may touch the caudal part of the arrow: then push out the arrow with that.
If the arrow is concave, then push out the arrow with an instrument entering into itself. The arrow will go out by itself.
If the arrow is poisonous, then it is necessary to cut away the entire piece of flesh in which the poison is, if this is possible Then care for the arrow as it deserves which is suitable for it
If the arrow has fallen into the chest, or the belly, or the back, or the side: and it is close to that which you touch with your hand, and it is possible to cut above that: then cut above that, and burn away from the incision of the vein, or nerve, and draw out the arrow.
Then, if necessary, take a pulse, and care for it until it heals.

On the phlebotomy of veins
The veins which are usually phlebotomized in the body are thirty in number
Of these, in the head there are sixty: two pulse veins, which are behind the ears, are called Herbae; two arteries which appear in two temporal regions; two veins which are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called Aspicientes; a vein prepared in the middle of the forehead; and a vein which is at the tip of the nose And two guide veins which are in the neck And two veins which are in the upper lip of the mouth And two veins which are in the lower lip. And these are the veins which are called Algecherich. And two veins which are under the tongue
For the veins which are phlebotomized in the arms, there are five veins in every arm.
One of them is the Cephalic, and it is from the side of the shoulder: and it names the great vein of the head And the Fusca And it is the Middle vein, and it is composed of the branch of the Basilic vein, and the branch of the Cephalic vein: and it names the great vein of the body And the Basilic, and it is placed on the domestic side: and it is also called the Titillicaris. And it names the great vein of the abdomen And the Brachial vein, and it is placed above the elbow: and it is that in which phlebotomy is done, and that which appears above the thumb with a visible swelling.
And the Palateal: and it is the vein which is between the ankle and the heel: and there are two branches to it.
And in the leg and in the foot there are three veins. One of them is which is under the curvature of the thumb from the side of the shoulder. And the second is the Saphenous: and its place is alongside the calcaneus from the domestic side And the Great Saphenous: and its place is alongside the calcaneus from the shoulder side
And on the other leg there are three veins like these
After the Aures, perform a phlebotomy of two veins.
After the Aures, perform a phlebotomy of two veins which are post Aures, for treatment of ancient cataracts, and migraine, and sapafi, and old head ulcer.
The quality of the phlebotomy is according to what is narrated. And it is that the head of the patient should be relaxed: and one should press the area of the two veins with a rough cloth with good friction Then let the patient tighten his neck with his hands, until two veins appear. And their places are post Aures in two depressed places of the head. Seek therefore easily with your finger, and where you feel their pulse under your finger, there is the sign with the imprint.
Then take the phlebotomy knife, which is called Incidens Then introduce it under the vein into the skin, until the phlebotomist reaches the bone. Then lift your hand with the vein and skin towards the upper parts, and cut the vein with the incision which is incidental And the length of the incision is the quantity of two joined fingers, or thereabouts: and let blood flow out as much as you wish
Then bind the patient with bands, and let go of the vein, until it is healed
And thus it is at the beginning of this book that the incisions and the cauterization of the veins are mentioned.</start_of_turn>

Then lift the skin over the vein upwards with thy index finger, and make the incision below, and elevate the vein upwards. And cut through it, like thou didst in two other veins: and cause the blood to flow according to the quantity which thou shalt need.
Then loosen the clotting of the patient, and place thy finger over the vein for an hour. Then place over it the cushion and the pillows, and bind it tightly above the constriction: and let it go, until it is healed

Of the phlebotomy of veins according to Algeberich The veins of Algeberich are phlebotomized because they cause vomiting at the root of the tongue, corruption of the gums: and sores of the lips, and wounds in the nose, and in the surrounding area

Of the phlebotomy of the vein under the tongue after the phlebotomy of the Cephalic veins The veins under the tongue are useful for phlebotomy: for it is the cephalic vein which is useful for the affections of the gut, and of the tongue, and of the mouth.
The quality of the phlebotomy which is useful is that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun: and raise his tongue, and look under the tongue at one side a vein, and at the other side a vein: and the colour of both veins should incline towards blackness.
Phlebotomy is therefore useful on both sides: and take care, do not put your last hand in phlebotomy. For under these are arteries, and perhaps there will be a flow of blood from these arteries.
The three veins which are phlebotomized in the elbow are such that phlebotomy is usual in all men.
And phlebotomy of them is done in two ways. Either by pressing with the thumb alongside phlebotomy: or by lancing with oil to the point of blueness: or by cutting with a knife, and this is Alnesil. This is its form.
And there are wide and narrow species according to the width of the veins and the tension of them. The form of phlebotomy of the thumb is wide, like water And it is suitable for opening wide veins, full of blood, protruding, visible, large, and those which contain thick blood
And this phlebotomy is of smaller width and greater fineness
It is suitable for phlebotomy of slender veins which contain thin yellow blood.

Because they draw blood from the swellings which are under the jaw and the throat, from that which follows the chest, and the belly: and it is suitable for the phlebotomist as well as for the patient, as it is above the risk of that there is an artery there If, therefore, it goes wrong, and there is an error in the puncture of the phlebotomy, the artery will be injured, and there will be a flow of blood Therefore it is necessary not to do phlebotomy with the phlebotomist who is puncturing: but rather to do it dry like Alnesil.

If the blood spurts at the phlebotomy, like the urine of a child, and is thin and red: then you know that it is from an artery. On the usefulness of Phlebotomy, and precautions to be observed in its practice. The quality of Phlebotomy, and the accidents that arise from it, require consideration in their rectification.
Firstly, know that Phlebotomy is not to be employed except for the conservation of health, and for the preservation of life, and with caution against the hazards.
And that it should be performed only on the three veins that are in the elbow, namely the Cephalica, and the Fusca, and the Basilica. And that it should be performed at the beginning of spring after fasting, in summer, and autumn, and in winter after a meal, when there are signs of fullness
It should be performed on the first or third day after three hours have passed
Phlebotomy for ailments has no set time: but when it is convenient and necessary for this, in the night or day, and at every hour, and at every time.
And it should not be performed on children until they are at least fourteen years of age. Neither should it be performed on a pregnant woman except from the fourth month until the seventh Nor on the elderly who have passed their sixties years.
When anyone wishes to undergo Phlebotomy for whatever reason: it is necessary to loosen his bowels beforehand with a laxative, if there is much retained stool: so that they do not draw blood from the veins with the remnants of putrid feces adhering to the principal limbs
Neither should it be performed on a feverish patient, that is, one with nausea: nor on a drunkard, or one suffering from intoxication until these symptoms have passed from the body Neither the infirm nor the healthy suffer from hydropisi.
